Now, after a dozen more games and becoming a top mobile publisher, Voodoo comes out with the sequel.\r\n\r\npaperio_icon_comparison.png\r\nI'm going to take a look at Paper.io 2 from a game design perspective. I will look at the overall flow of the game, the design of the difficulty curve, and a psychological trick that will keep players coming back.\r\n\r\nBasic Description\r\nThe objective of the game is to control 100% of the arena. You play as a small, ever moving square with a small starting territory that corresponds to your square's color.\r\n\r\nThere are other players that start the same way and have the same goal.\r\n\r\nIn your own territory, you are safe. When you leave, you create a trail that draws onto the arena. If you make it back to your territory then you gain control of the territory you just traversed.\r\n\r\nIf someone else hits your trail, you die, your territory is lost, and you must start over. \r\n\r\nA major difference between Paper.io 2 and the original is how you move. In the original, you could only move in 4 directions: up, down, left, and right. Now you can move in any direction. The arena is now circular instead of square to complement that change.\r\n\r\nThe game starts with a screen displaying your current character and your high score, which is displayed as a percentage of the highest area you have conquered.\r\n\r\nYou may select any characters you have unlocked and then start the game.\r\n\r\nYou conquer territory and kill other players until you die. Canadian English), also called American checkers or Straight checkers, is a form of the strategy board game draughts\r\n\r\nMove rules\r\nThere are two different ways to move in English draughts:\r\nA simple move consists of moving a piece one square diagonally to an adjacent unoccupied dark square. Uncrowned pieces can move only diagonally forward; kings can move in any diagonal direction.\r\nA jump consists of moving a piece from a square diagonally adjacent to an opponent's piece, to an empty square immediately beyond it in the same direction. (Thus jumping over the opponent's piece.) Uncrowned pieces can jump only diagonally forward; kings can jump in any diagonal direction. A jumped piece is considered \"captured\" and removed from the game. Any piece, whether crowned or not, can jump a king.\r\nMultiple jumps are possible, if after one jump, another piece is immediately eligible to be jumped—even if that jump is in a different diagonal direction. If more than one multiple-jump move is available, the player can choose which piece to jump with, and which sequence of jumps to make. The jumping sequence chosen is not required to be the one that maximizes the number of jumps in the turn; however, a player must make all available jumps in the sequence chosen.\r\nJumping is always mandatory: if a player has the option to jump, he must take it, even if doing so results in disadvantage for the jumping player. For example, a mandated single jump might set up the player such that the opponent has a multi-jump in reply.\r\n\r\nThe best board game that does not require any special representation.
